<i>Ang-[=á]ng na run igikan. Dì na ka kaabut,</i> It's
no use going now. You'll never make it. <i>Ang-[=á]ng
iadtu run kay sayu pa,</i> No use going so
early. <b>2</b> not quite the right amount. <i>Alang-álang
pa ning kwartang ilukat sa prinda,</i> This
money is insufficient to pay off the mortgage.
<i>Ang-[=á]ng ning panaptúna pára karsúnis,</i>
This is not enough cloth for a pair of
pants. <b>3</b> not up to a certain level. <i>Ang-[=á]ng
pagkapanday,</i> It was poorly done. <i>Sumbágun
ta untà ka, apan ang-[=á]ng ka ra nákù,</i> I
would love to fight you, but you're too
small for me. <b>4</b> @somewhat, but not quite.
<i>Ang lamì alang-álang nangkà, alang-álang
pinya,</i> The taste is somewhat like jackfruit,
somewhat like pineapple. <i>n</i> <b>1</b> it would be
silly if, it would be the wrong thing to do if.
<i>Ang-[=á]ng dílì dawátun. Gihátag man,</i> It
would be silly not to accept it. It was given
to you, wasn't it? <i>Ang-[=á]ng akuy manghúgas
nga náa may masúgù,</i> Why should I do
the dishes when there's s.o. I can tell to do
them. <b>2</b> of course. <i>'Malígù ka?'--'Ang-[=á]ng.
Mau bitaw nay átung gianhi,'</i> 'Are you going
to swim?'--'Of course, that's what we
came here for, isn't it?' <i>v</i> [A; b5c1] <b>1</b> do
s.t. poorly, halfway. <i>Ug alang-alángun (alang-alángan,
ialang-álang) nà nímug búhat,
ay na lang,</i> If you're going to do a poor
job, never mind. <b>2</b> do s.t. at an inopportune
time. <i>Dílì pa ku run mualang-álang ug
minyù nga walà kuy salapì,</i> I'm not going
to go and get married at this time when I
don't have any money. <b>3</b> [B256N; b4(1)]
arrive a little too late or early for s.t. <i>Mangang-[=á]ng
kug larga,</i> I'll leave a bit ahead.
<b>4</b> [b4] lacking s.t. <i>Naang-ángan ku sa kwarta,</i>
I am short of money. <b>5</b> [ab2] be put in
a difficult situation by s.t. inopportune. <i>Ímu
kung alang-alángug pangutána nga náa may
láing namátì,</i> You put me in a difficult situation
asking that question when s.o. else is
listening. <b>6</b> [A23] have hesitations about
doing s.t. <i>Dílì giyud aku mualang-álang nímug
pangutánag dílì pa tinúud,</i> I wouldn't
have reservations about asking you if it
weren't true. <b>7</b> [b6] consider s.t. <i>alang-álang</i>.
<i>Giang-[=á]ngan aku sa íyang hitsúra,</i> I
consider his looks not up to par. <i>Giang-[=á]ngan
akug hangyù níya,</i> It's a bad time for
me to ask him. <b>(->)</b> = <sc>ALANG-ÁLANG</sc>, <i>v</i>, <i>a3</i>.

to get? <i>Iambug ning kamúti arun ibaligyà,</i>

is overlooking the edge of the cliff. <b>pa-</b> <i>v</i>
[a] build s.t. so it overlooks. <i>Gipaambug ku
ang ámung payag sa ngilit sa pangpang,</i> I

sa násud,</i> He has much to contribute to the
development of the country. <b>2</b> contribute
to increase the intensity or quality. <i>Ang kaígang
nakaámut sa íyang kapungut,</i> The
heat contributed to making his anger worse.
<b>-l-an, -l-an(->)</b> <i>n</i> @contribution. <i>Pagkadaghag
alamútan (alamutan) sa iskuylahan, makapubri!</i>
You can go broke with all the contributions
you have to make in school.

<b>amúti</b> = <sc>KAMÚTI</sc>.

<b>ámuy_{1}</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> @icon. <b>2</b> the name of @God used in
speaking to small children. <i>Ayaw pangáway
kay masukù ang ámuy,</i> Don't quarrel because
God will get angry.

<b>ámuy_{2}</b> <i>n</i> term of address for very old men
of respectability. <i>Kanà si Ámuy Militun kapitan
sa panahun sa Katsílà,</i> Amoy Meliton
was a village head during the Spanish times.
<i>v</i> [a12] call s.o. Amoy.

<b>amyun</b> <i>v</i> [BN] @emit a sweet fragrance. <i>Miamyun
(nangamyun) ang kahumut sa mga búlak,</i>
The flowers emitted a sweet fragrance.
<b>ka-</b> <i>n</i> @{sweet smell}.

<b>-an_{1}</b> local passive verb affix, future. (<i>past</i> <b>gi-an</b>; [**hyphen should stay]
<i>subjunctive</i> <b>-i</b>. <i>Potential forms: past</i> <b>na-an</b>; [**hyphen should stay]
<i>future</i> <b>ma-an</b> or, alternatively, <b>ka-an</b>;
<i>subjunctive</i> <b>ma-i</b> or, alternatively, <b>ka-i</b>.) Not
all verbs occur with this affix, and those
that do may occur with only one or two or
all of the meanings. <b>1</b> [do] for, at, on, in.
<i>Palitan ku siyag kík,</i> I will buy him cake (or
buy cake from him). <i>Gipalitan ku siya,</i> I
bought some for (from) him. <i>Wà ku siya
paliti,</i> I didn't buy any for (from) him. <i>Mapalitan
(kapalitan) ku siya,</i> I can buy some
for (from) him. <i>Napalitan ku siya,</i> I managed
to buy some for (from) him. <i>Wà ku siya
mapaliti (kapaliti),</i> I couldn't buy any
for (from) him. <b>1a</b> <i>with noun bases:</i> give,
provide s.o. [noun]. <i>Sirúhan ka nákù,</i> I will
give you a zero. <i>Sapatúsan ku ang bátà,</i> I
will put shoes on the child. <b>2</b> [do] directly
to s.o. or s.t. <i>Hagkan ku ikaw,</i> I will kiss
you. <i>Bantayan ninyu ang prísu,</i> Watch the
prisoner. <b>2a</b> [do] to part of s.t. <i>Kuháan ku
ang ímung kík ug gamay,</i> I will take a little
of your cake. <i>Kunhúran ku ang prisyu,</i> I
will take a little off the price. <b>3</b> <i>with verbs
from adjectives:</i> consider s.t. as. <i>Lisdan siya
sa átung sinultihan,</i> He will find our language
difficult. <i>Gipilahan ka lang uruy niánà?</i>
Do you consider that a small amount?
<b>4</b> have [verb] happen to one. <i>Naulanan
aku,</i> I was caught in the rain. <i>Labdan ka sa
úlu,</i> You will get a headache. (It will happen
to you that your head will ache.) <b>5</b>
-----File: 0098.png---\jhellingman\TIMP\triggerhippie77\Long Green\\-------
[do] because of, due to. <i>Unsay gihilákan
mu?</i> What is it you are crying about? <i>Díli[**typo: Dílì][**P3: ` accent on 2nd "i" seems to be cut off in scan; see "l" before it]
nà ángayng kabalak-an,</i> That is not worth
getting worried over. <b>6</b> do in [such-and-such
a manner]. <i>Usaan nà nákug alsa,</i> I will
lift that with one (hand). <i>Datadatáhan ku
nag báyad,</i> I will pay for that in installments.
<b>7</b> work off a debt, pay for by [do]-*ing.
<i>Mahímù nímung trabahúan ang ímung
útang nákù,</i> You may work off your debt
to me. <i>Buk-an kug lubi kining bugas,</i> I'll
pay for this rice by splitting coconuts.

<b>-an_{2}</b> suffix forming verb bases to which the
prefixes <i>mag-</i>, <i>tig-</i> and <i>pag-</i> may be added.
The verb with these affixes always has
stress on the final syllable and means '[do]
s.t. at a certain place habitually'. <i>Mag-anhian
siya dinhig maduminggu,</i> He comes here
on Sundays. <i>Siyay tig-anhian dinhi,</i> He
comes here often. <i>Sa ímung pag-adtuan didtu,
nakailaíla kag usa ka Mang Tiryu?</i> In
the times you've been going to that place,
did you ever meet a certain Mang Terio?

<b>-an_{3}</b> noun forming affix. <b>1</b> forming nouns
which refer to a place where s.t. is found,
done, held, located. <i>Humayan,</i> Rice field.
<i>Tubaan,</i> Place where toddy is sold. <i>Baskitbulan,</i>
Place [**missing "where"|F1 not needed]basketball is played. <i>Habagatan,</i>
West (place from which the <i>habágat</i>
'west wind' blows). <i>Bairan,</i> Sharpener (thing
on which one sharpens). <i>Tindáhan,</i> Store
(place [**missing "where"]one sells). <b>2</b> forming nouns which
refer to a person possessed of a certain
power. Nouns of this sort always have long
penults. <i>Tambálan,</i> Folk doctor. <i>Hilútan,</i>
Doctor specializing in massage. <i>Barángan,</i>
A sorcerer with magic insects at his disposal.

<b>-an_{4}</b> adjective forming affix. <b>1</b> forming adjectives
which mean 'characterized by being
[so-and-so]'. Words of this sort have the
stress on the final syllable. <i>Langasan,</i> Of a
noisy type. <i>Talawan,</i> Cowardly. <i>Gahian,</i> Of
a hard sort. <b>2</b> added to nouns to form adjectives
which mean 'having [so-and-so]'.
<i>Utúkan,</i> Brainy. <i>Kwartáhan,</i> Moneyed.

<b>-an(->)</b> short for <b>hi-an(->)</b>.

<b>-an-</b> infix optionally added to all forms with
the prefixes <i>nag-</i>, <i>mag-</i>, <i>pag-</i>, indicating that
affixed forms refer to more than one person.
<i>Nanagsábut sila,</i> They made (plurally)
an agreement. <i>Duha ka managsúun,</i> Two
brothers. <i>Ang ílang panagsábut,</i> Their (plural)
agreement with each other.

<b>an[=à]</b> <b>1</b> expression of surprise. <b>a</b> at s.t. pleasant.
<i>An[=à], kanindut sa ímung ariyus,</i> Oh
what beautiful earrings you have! <b>b</b> at s.t.
which causes worry. <i>An[=à]! Nabuak,</i> Oh-Oh!
It broke. <b>2</b> expression chiding s.o. <i>An[=à]!</i>
-----File: 0099.png---\jhellingman\TIMP\triggerhippie77\Long Green\\-------
<i>Nagpabuyag man ka!</i> My! You're making
a nuisance of yourself.

<b>ánà</b> = <sc>NIÁNÀ</sc>. <i>see</i> <sc>KANÀ</sc>.

<b>anáa</b> <i>short form</i>: <b>náa</b>. <b>1</b> be @there (near you).
<i>Náa ba dihà ang yáwi?</i> Do you have (is
there) the key? <b>1a</b> be employed at, work
at. <i>Náa siya sa Atlas,</i> He works for Atlas.
<i>Náa ra siya sa báy,</i> He is always at home.
<b>2</b> there is. <i>Náay suwat pára nímu,</i> There is
a letter for you. <b>3a --</b> <i>dat.</i> [dat.] @has. <i>Náa
kaníya ang yáwi,</i> He has the key. <b>3b</b> it depends
upon [dat.]. <i>Náa ra nímug muadtu
ta,</i> It's up to you if we should go. <b>3c</b> be
menstruating. <i>Dílì mudúul ang bána ug náa
sa asáwa,</i> A husband cannot have intercourse
with his wife when she is menstruating.
<b>4</b> <b>unsa may -- niánà, sa</b> [<i>noun</i>]?
what does that, [noun] have to do with it?
<i>Unsa ba guy náa sa idad?</i> And what does
age have to do with it? <b>pagka-</b> <i>n</i> the state
of being there. <i>Ang íyang pagkaanáa sa balay,</i>
His presence in the house. <b>paka-</b> <i>v</i> [A13;[**joined up "[A1" & "3;"]
a12] strive to have s.t. <i>Ímu kung pakaanaáhun
bisan[**bísan] wà kuy nahut,</i> You try to get
s.t. from me even though I haven't anything.
<b>anaáhun</b> <i>a</i> well-to-do.

<b>ánab</b> (from <i>bána</i>) <i>n</i> @husband (slang).

<b>anabyung</b> = <sc>HINAGDUNG</sc>.

<b>ánad</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B23(1); b(1)] take to, become

s.t. <i>Muánad (maánad) siyag panghilabut sa

When you get used to the work, you won't

<b>-anan_{1}</b> affix added to verbs to form nouns
which have meanings analogous to the meanings
of the local passive verbs. Cf. <b>-AN_{1}</b>. <b>1</b>
place or person for whom s.t. is done. <i>Palitánan
sa bugas,</i> Place [**missing "where"]one buys rice. <i>Lingkuránan,</i>
Seat. <i>Hatagánan sa limus,</i> Persons to
whom the alms are given. <b>2</b> thing to which
s.t. is to be done. <i>Labhanan,</i> Wash to be
done. <i>Handumánan,</i> Keepsake (thing which
one thinks back on).

<b>-anan_{2}(->)</b> alternant of <i>-an_{2}</i> used with roots
that have a short penultimate vowel that
is dropped on suffixation. <i>Maghagkanan sa
tiil sa birhin,</i> They kiss the feet of the
Virgin.

<b>an-an</b> <i>n</i> k.o. small tree of thickets: <b><i>Buchanania
arborescens</i></b>.

<b>ananaklaw</b> (from <i>saklaw</i>) <i>n</i> k.o. tiny house
spider that jumps on its prey.

<b>ananakyud</b> (from <i>sakyud</i>) <i>n</i> k.o. bird of the
seashore that moves its buttocks up and
down.

<b>ananamsi</b> <i>n</i> k.o. small timber tree.

<b>anananggal</b> <i>n</i> k.o. <i>unglù</i> who, when under his[**his? An anananggal's female.]
supernatural spell, detaches the portion of
his body above the waist from the lower
portion and flies away with trailing intestines
in search of his prey, leaving the lower
portion. This detachment occurs only at
night, and the <i>anananggal</i> dies if the sun
strikes any portion of the separated body.
He can also be killed by putting salt on the
lower portion. <i>see also</i> <sc>TANGGAL</sc>.

<b>ananangkil</b> (from <i>sangkil</i>) <i>n</i> k.o. small hawk
with black and brown speckles on a light
brown and white background.

<b>anapug</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> k.o. soft shale. <b>2</b> soft coral rock.
<b>-an</b> <i>n</i> place where there is shale or coral
rock. <b>-un</b> <i>a</i> full of shale, coral rock.

<b>ánas</b> <i>v</i> [B; c1] @landslide. <i>Muánas (maánas)

<b>ánaw_{2}</b> <i>n</i> area of the surface of the sea which

area, usually visible when the sea is

<b>anay_{1}</b> (from <i>ina</i>) <i>n</i> <b>1</b> @sow. <b>2</b> woman that is a

<b>andu, andù_{1}</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A1; a12] expect to realize

<b>2</b> [A; a] @{sum up}, make an account of. <i>Nag-andu
siya sa mga butang nga wà gánì níya
mahímu,</i> She is counting up things for credit
to get credit for them, when she hasn't
even done them. <i>Ayaw kug paningli, kay ug

kabayad,</i> Do not try to collect what I owe
you, because if we sum up all that I spent
on you, you could never pay. <b>3</b> [A; b4(1)]
lay open one's cards. <i>Kun makaandu na ka,
dì ka na makapunù,</i> When you have already
laid your cards on the table, you cannot add
any more cards. <b>3a pag- (inig-) pa</b> but actually,
when it came (comes) to the test (when
the cards were laid on the table). <i>Sígi siyang
hangyù. Pag-andù pa, dì diay gustu,</i> He kept
begging, but when I finally agreed to it, he
didn't want to. <i>Padatùdátù siya. Pag-andù
pa, pubri kaáyu,</i> He pretended to be rich.
But when it came to the test, he turned out
to be poor. <i>n</i> <b>way --</b> @{not certain}. <i>Wà pay
andu ug maghíkay ba mi sa pyista,</i> We're
undecided as yet whether to prepare for the
fiesta. <b>andúhay</b> <i>n</i> @confrontation. <i>v</i> [C] have
a confrontation. <i>Mag-andúhay ta arun mahúsay

<i>Anduhúnun pa ning ákung pagpaiskuyla

<i>Angkub ang ímung paghátag kanámù sa diriksiyun,</i>

<b>angkun</b> <i>v</i> [A; a12] claim as one's own, @admit
authorship of an act. <i>Dì siya muangkun
nga siyay may salà,</i> He will not admit that
he is wrong. <i>Kinsay nag-angkun nga iyáha

is his? <b>2</b> [A2; a12] @acquire, @get as one's

naangkun,</i> This is my lot in life. <b>2a</b> [A23]
be in a certain situation. <i>Dílì siya gustung
muangkun sa kinabúhing pinubri,</i> He does
not want to lead the life of a poor man. <b>3</b>
[A3; a12] take as one's share of contributions
or responsibility. <i>Akuy muangkun sa
ilimnun,</i> I'll take care of the drinks. <i>Angkúnun
ku ang panghúgas sa plátu,</i> I'll take

<b>ap-andawun</b> <i>n</i> the situation in a game of
mahjong where to obtain mahjong (go out)
the player needs to complete only a single
straight (sequences of three pieces in numerical
order) such that either the lower number
of the higher number will complete the
sequence. E.g., if a player is complete for
mahjong except for one straight for which
he has only the pieces five and six, he needs
either seven or four to make the straight
complete and get mahjong, and thus he is
in the <i>ap-andawun</i> situation.

He wasn't crying. What did you have to

gipugus. Naapil ku sa kasábà,</i> I didn't
want to go with you, but you forced me.
Now I got in trouble along with you. <i>n</i> action
of saying '<i>apat</i>'. <i>Walay apat nga mag-una,</i>
The <i>apat</i> ('it would have been better')
always comes afterwards.

<b>ay_{1}</b> <b>1</b> expression dismissing what follows as

ulahi ka na, nahurut na ug kahálin,</i> Oh you
are too late. They're all sold out. <i>Ay, kapait
ning kinabuhía,</i> My, how difficult life is.
<b>3</b> particle preceding an exclamation of delight.
<i>Ay, kanindut sa búlak!</i> Oh, what a

-----File: 0159.png---\Ecronotics\jhellingman\triggerhippie77\Long Green\\-
<i>*kù,</i> Teacher, Pedro was making faces at me.

<b>ay_{4}</b> <i>n</i> a pair of mahjong pieces of the same
number and design. In order to get mahjong,
a set must contain an <i>ay</i>.

<b>-ay_{1}</b> affix forming verbs which refer <b>1</b> to
reciprocal actions. <i>Naglalisay sila,</i> They argued
back and forth. <i>Nagtutukay sila,</i> They
stared at each other. <i>Naghigugmáay sila,</i>
They were in love with one another. <b>2</b> to
intense actions. <i>Naghilákay sila,</i> They cried
and cried. <i>Naghikayay sila kay pista ugmà,</i>
They were busy preparing because the fiesta
was the following day.

<b>-ay_{2}</b> affix added to verbs to form nouns referring
to manner in which s.t. is done.
<i>Maghúlin ta, bihagay,</i> Let's play marbles
for keeps (in the manner of <i>bíhag</i> 'capture').
<i>Magtínis ta, sirbisahay,</i> Let's play
tennis. The loser buys beer (lit. in the beer
manner). <i>Tagsingkwinta ang gatus, way piliay,</i>
They cost fifty a hundred, but no
choosing.

B


<b>ba</b> <b>1</b> question marker used in questions with
no interrogative. <i>Muanhi ka ba ugmà?</i> Will
you come here tomorrow? <b>1a</b> <i>with indirect
questions:</i> @whether. <i>Pangutan-a si Husi ug
nahinumdum ba siya,</i> Ask José if he remembers
it. <b>1b</b> was it [so-and-so]? <i>Písus ba tu
ímung gihátag nákù?</i> Was it a peso you
gave me? <b>2</b> <b>dì, dílì --</b> <b>2a</b> isn't that the case?
<i>Mulikù ta sa tuu, dì ba?</i> We turn right,
don't we? <b>2b</b> [so-and-so] is surely going to
be the consequence. <i>Hilabti nang makinilya.
Dì ba latiguhun tika,</i> Just touch that
typewriter. You think I'm not going to
smack you one? <b>3</b> <i>with interrogatives:</i> particle
indicating impatience or a strong questioning
tone. <i>Pila bay plíti?</i> How much is
-----File: 0167.png---\Ecronotics\jhellingman\triggerhippie77\jhellingman\\
it now? <b>unsa --</b> what do you say? how
about it? <i>Unsa ba, palitun nátù tung awtu?</i>
How about it? Shall we buy that car? <b>--
gud</b> particle indicating disbelief. <i>Mangáwat
ba gud ku?</i> Do you think I would steal?
<b>4</b> shall we say? <i>Muanhi ka ug sayu ugmà,
mga alas sayis ba,</i> Come here early tomorrow,
shall we say, six o'clock? <b>5</b> <b><sc>X</sc> -- <sc>Y</sc> --</b>
either <sc>X</sc> or <sc>Y</sc>. <i>Muanhi ka dáyun. Pagkaugmà
ba, sa sunud adlaw ba,</i> Come here as soon
as possible. Either the next day or the day
after that. <b>6</b> particle asking if the hearer
understands. <i>Si Mistir Krus tu, ag maistru
ba,</i> That was Mr. Cruz, the teacher, you
know. <i>Sugkáyun, pára ba maáyung pagkaságul,</i>
Stir it so, you know, it will get well-*
-----File: 0168.png---\Ecronotics\jhellingman\triggerhippie77\jhellingman\\
*mixed. <b>7</b> <i>in exclamations:</i> <b>7a</b> how unbelievable
that it is that way! <i>Pagkabúang ba
gayud nákù,</i> How could I be so foolish! <b>7b</b>
though. <i>Itusmaw sa ínit nga túbig? Pagkamakalulúuy
ba sab,</i> Throw it into boiling
water? How pitiful! <b>laliman ka --</b> can you
beat that! <i>Laliman ka ba niánà! Bayran
ang tulu ka awtu ug kás!</i> Can you beat
that! Paying cash for the three cars! <b>tíaw

<b>-- krawud</b> <i>n</i> proletariat (those
wearing <i>bakyà</i>).

<b>bakyánu</b> <i>a</i> @skillful, @adept. <i>Bakyánu nang batáa
sa pamakak,</i> That child fibs pretty well.
<i>v</i> [B1] be skillful, adept. <i>Magbakyánu ka
sa pagmakinilya arun makaimpliyar ka dáyun,</i>
Get adept at typing so you can find a
job right away.

<b>bakyaw</b> <i>v</i> [A; c] @swing the arm to strike a
blow.

<b>bala, bála_{1}</b> (not without <i>l</i>) <i>n</i> <b>1</b> @bullet. <b>2</b> @staples.
<b>3</b> @money. <i>v</i> [A; c] <b>1</b> load gun, stapler.
<i>Maáyu lang kang ibála sa kaniyun,</i> You are
just good for cannon fodder. <b>2a</b> put s.t. in
s.t. to make it appear bigger or weightier.
<i>Ang kupras baláhag balas,</i> The copra was
mixed with sand. <b>2b</b> @mix s.t. in with s.t. else
to hide it. <i>Ang pinaldung panaptun gibaláhag
sigarilyu,</i> The bales of cloth had cigarettes
hidden inside of them. <b>balahan</b> <i>a</i>
@loaded. <i>Pagbantay kay balahan nang pistúla,</i>
Be careful. That pistol is loaded.

<b>bála_{2}</b> <i>v</i> [A; a12] @carry s.t. on the back, not
tied. <i>Akuy mubála nímu inigtabuk sa sapà,</i>
I'll carry you piggy-back when we cross
the river. <i>Baláha (balha) kanang sáku,</i> Carry
that sack on your back. <b>gi- gilukdu</b> full of
happiness, mischief, worries, and other emotions
(lit. carried on the back and on the
head). <i>Ang gwatsi ánang tawhána gibá gilukdu,</i>
That man is chock-full of mischief.

<b>balà_{1}</b> (not without <i>l</i>) <i>v</i> [A; a12] find out information
about an event that has happened
(who stole s.t., where s.t. stolen or lost
is, who committed a crime, etc.) by means
of an egg. The egg is made to stand on its
end on the edge of a tumbler. Then a yes-no
question is put to it. If the answer is yes,
the egg remains upright. If the answer is no,
the egg falls. <i>Balaun ang bábuy kay sigúrung
gikáwat tu,</i> We'll @divine information
about the pig, because it surely was stolen.
<b>balad-un</b> <i>n</i> @omen, a sign which prophesizes
s.t. <i>Ang kumíta mauy usa ka bad-un nga
may umaábut nga kagúbut,</i> A comet is a
sign of a forthcoming war. <b>tiking balad-un</b>
phrase used to address the gecko (house
lizard) in asking him to foretell whether s.t.
will happen. The question is put to the
gecko before he sounds. After he sounds
the question is repeated. If the gecko sounds
-----File: 0200.png---\jhellingman\TIMP\triggerhippie77\gegenueber\\-------
an odd number of times the answer is affirmative.
If even, the answer is negative. <i>Tiking
balad-un, muulan ugmà?</i> Prophet gecko,
will it rain tomorrow?

<b>balà_{2}</b> = <sc>BALÁLÀ.</sc>

<b>bálà</b> (not without <i>l</i>) <i>v</i> [A; c] warn so as to
prohibit certain actions. <i>Gibaláan na man
mu,</i> You have been warned and prohibited.
<i>Úsà ka mamusil sa háyup ibálà úsà,</i> Before
you start shooting stray animals, make a
warning prohibiting it. <i>n</i> warning that prohibits.

<b>baláan</b> <i>a</i> @holy, @sacred. <i>Gahum sa mga baláan,</i>
Power of the saints. <b>paka-</b> <i>v</i> [a12] considered
sacred. <i>Gipakabaláan sa mga bumbay
ang báka,</i> The Hindus considered the cow a
sacred animal. <b>-un</b> @saintly. <i>Balaánun ang
ákung tingúhà kanímu,</i> I have noble intentions
toward you.

<b>baláat</b> <i>v</i> [A; a] @tie s.t. around s.t. <i>Baátun ta
ning sugnud,</i> Let's bundle the firewood. <i>Baáti
íyang bàbà arun dì kasyágit,</i> Gag her
mouth so she can't shout. <i>n</i> s.t. tied around
s.t.

<b>balábag</b> <i>v</i> [AA2S[**double A?]; c1] <b>1</b> lie across a path.
<i>Balabágun (ibábag) nátù pagbutang ang káhuy,</i>
Let's put the tree across the road. <i>Gibabágan
ang agiánan sa mga batu,</i> The path
was blocked by rocks. <b>2</b> block s.o.'s way.
<i>Ikaw ray nakabábag sa ákung kalípay,</i> You
are the only one who stands in the way of
my happiness. <b>3</b> for a fetus to be in a transverse
position. <i>Naglísud siya pag-anak kay
nagbalábag (nagbalabag) ang bátà,</i> She had
a hard labor because the child was in a
transverse position. <i>n</i> <b>1</b> a piece of wood or
metal which lies across s.t. <i>Ang balabag mauy
naglambing sa duha ka kasku,</i> The cross-*beam
holds the two hulls of the boat together.
<b>2</b> cross (not without <i>l</i> in this meaning).
<i>Gilansang si Hisus sa balábag,</i> Jesus
was nailed to a cross. <b>3</b> s.t. which bars the
way. <i>Dílì balábag sa hangtúray nílang panaghigála,</i>
It is not a bar to their eternal
friendship. <b>(->)</b> <i>n</i> = <sc>BALÁBAG,</sc> <i>n.</i>[**period?] <b>-an(->)</b> <i>n</i>
@fishes with a transverse line, e.g., k.o. snappers.

<b>balabála</b> <i>n</i> a children's game played by hitting
a ball one tosses himself with a stick. If another
player catches the ball, he comes up
to bat. <i>v</i> [A1] play this game.

<b>baladaw</b> = <sc>BALARAW.</sc>

<b>baladbad</b> = <sc>BADBAD_{1}.</sc>

<b>baládin</b> (not without <i>l</i>) <i>n</i> wooden container
for palm toddy in the shape of a tapered
cylinder. <i>v</i> [A13; a12] make a wooden container
for palm toddy.

<b>balad-un</b> <i>see</i> <sc>BALÀ_{1}.</sc>
